{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"‘American Horror Story’ Season 10: Release Date, Cast and More","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683480","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-683488 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ahs10header-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ahs10header.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ahs10header-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><em>(Welcome to <a href=\"https://slashfilm.com/tag/and-more\"><strong>…And More</strong></a>, our no-frills, zero B.S. guide to when and where you can watch upcoming movies and shows, and everything else you could possibly stand to know.)</em></p>\n<p><strong>Ryan Murphy </strong>and <strong>Brad Falchuk</strong>&#8216;s horror anthology series, <em><strong>American Horror Story</strong></em><em>, </em>has somehow been running for 10 seasons. The often campy cult hit uses a rotating retinue of actors playing different characters each season, and it&#8217;s a lot of gross, gory fun. The first season, <em><strong>American Horror Story: Murder House </strong></em>debuted in 2011 and quickly gained notoriety for its wild storylines, taste for melodrama, and fantastic performances from some of genre&#8217;s finest. A decade later and the series is still going, having gone through every horror subgenre, from killer nuns and alien abductions in season 2&#8217;s <em><strong>Asylum</strong>,</em><em> </em>to the straight-up end of the world in season 8&#8217;s <em><strong>Apocalypse</strong></em><em>. </em>Here&#8217;s what we know about what&#8217;s in store for season 10 of this continually surprising series.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683480\"></span></p>\n<h2>American Horror Story Season 10 Release Date and Where You Can Watch It</h2>\n<p>The 10th season of Murphy and Falchuk&#8217;s deliciously sensationalist anthology series was supposed to debut in late 2020 but was delayed due to the coronavirus pandemic. Now, <em>American Horror Story</em> season 10 will premiere on FX in the U.S. on <strong>Wednesday, August 25</strong> at 10 p.m. EST, and will be available for streaming the next day on FX on Hulu. There&#8217;s no official listing of the number of episodes yet, but the previous seasons have all had between 10 and 13 episodes a piece, each debuting every week after the premiere. (So, basically, if you wanna be among the first to watch, you&#8217;ll need to set aside your Wednesday nights or Thursday mornings this fall!)</p>\n<h2>So What&#8217;s Season 10 Going to Be About?</h2>\n<p>Here&#8217;s where it&#8217;s all kind of weird guesswork, so bear with me. The <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/american-horror-story-season-10-poster/\">posters</a> and a <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CMni7mknbB4/?utm_source=ig_web_copy_link\">few cryptic Instagram comments from Murphy</a> about one story taking place in the sand and another taking place by the sea are really all we have to go on. Murphy has also confirmed on his Instagram that fans will be getting &#8220;two stories for the price of one,&#8221; so the <em>Double Feature </em>subtitle for this season appears to be quite literal. My best guess, given the poster and &#8220;by the sea and by the sand,&#8221; is that one story will focus on mermaids or sirens and be a nautical-themed horror story, and the other will be an Area 51/abduction type story, probably set in the American Southwest. Whether or not they&#8217;ll be connected by any story through-lines or we&#8217;re actually just getting two anthology stories in one season is anyone&#8217;s best guess.</p>\n<h2>What&#8217;s the Difference Between This and American Horror Stories?</h2>\n<p>It&#8217;s okay to be a little confused — the names are pretty similar. <em>American Horror Story</em> season 10 will continue in the vein of its previous seasons, with a single (or in this case, double) anthology story told over the course of the season. <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/american-horror-stories/\">The new spin-off series, <em><strong>American Horror Stories</strong></em></a>, will tell a different story each episode, more in the vein of something like <em><strong>Black Mirror</strong></em><strong> </strong>or <em><strong>The Twilight Zone</strong></em><em>. </em></p>\n<h2>American Horror Story Season 10 Cast</h2>\n<p>One thing <em>American Horror Story</em> has going for it is its huge rotating cast of genre and character-acting heavies. While fan favorites and regular players <strong>Emma Roberts</strong> and <strong>Jessica Lange </strong>are sitting this season out, there will be plenty of familiar faces for fans to get excited about. <strong>Sarah Paulson</strong>, who should basically crown herself queen of the franchise at this point, is back once more. <strong>Evan Peters</strong>, <strong>Kathy Bates</strong>, <strong>Billie Lourd</strong>,<strong> Finn Wittrock</strong>, <strong>Lily Rabe</strong>, <strong>Leslie Grossman</strong>, <strong>Adina Porter,</strong> and <strong>Angelica Ross </strong>will all return.</p>\n<p>Newcomers this season include model-actress <strong>Kaia Gerber</strong> and former child star and current internet personality <strong>Macaulay Culkin</strong>. Culkin&#8217;s joining the cast is honestly going to be the thing that makes me check out the newest season after the disappointment of the end of season eight and well, just skipping nine completely. While we don&#8217;t know what Culkin&#8217;s character is, we do know that <a href=\"https://ew.com/tv/american-horror-story-season-10-first-look-macaulay-culkin/\">he will have a &#8220;crazy erotic sex&#8221; scene with Bates</a>, which makes for must-see WTF TV.</p>\n<h2>American Horror Story Season 10 Special Poster</h2>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-683499\" The Answer Will Shock You, Unless It Doesn’t","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683272","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-69-1.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683382\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-69-1-700x325.jpg\" alt=\"Worst DCEU Movie\" width=\"700\" height=\"325\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-69-1-700x325.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-69-1-360x167.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/FotoJet-69-1-768x357.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><em>(Welcome to <strong>Survey Says</strong>, a feature where we conduct a movie-related survey for a random group of people and explain why they&#8217;re completely right, completely wrong, or somewhere in-between.)</em></p>\n<p>This is it, the 100% official, unquestionable and infallible answer to the ancient question: what is the worst DCEU movie? That&#8217;s right – there will be no disagreement here. These are solid <em>facts</em> backed up by <em>science</em>. And by <em>science,</em> I mean the website Survey Monkey. And if you can&#8217;t trust a monkey that runs its own surveys, who the hell can you trust?</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683272\"></span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Picture19.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683371\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Picture19-700x422.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"422\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Picture19-700x422.png 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Picture19-360x217.png 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Picture19-768x463.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>By the Numbers</strong></h2>\n<p>Before we go any further, I must stress that the results of this survey come from 613 respondents in the United States. So&#8230;you know, it&#8217;s not really that exact. On top of that, this survey is flawed because it completely omits<em> <strong>Suicide Squad</strong></em>, <em><strong>Birds of Prey,</strong> </em>and <strong><em>Shazam!</em></strong> At first I thought that this survey just must be old and outdated – but no. The Snyder Cut, AKA <strong><em>Zack Snyder&#8217;s Justice League</em></strong>, is on here, and so is <strong><em>Wonder Woman 1984</em></strong>, and both of those came out after <em>Suicide Squad</em>, <em>Birds of Prey,</em> and <em>Shazam!</em> Meaning that when the Survey Monkey swung down from his tree with bananas on his breath to put this survey together, he really goofed up. Smooth move, Mr. Monkey. Go back into your tree and think about what you did.</p>\n<p>Anyway, now that that&#8217;s out of the way, let&#8217;s take a look at the numbers, shall we? Here are the Worst DCEU Movies, according to this easy-to-ignore survey.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Batman v Superman 22.19%</li>\n<li>Snyder Cut 21.37%</li>\n<li>Justice League 14.68%</li>\n<li>Wonder Woman 1984 13.70%</li>\n<li>Aquaman 11.42%</li>\n<li>Man of Steel 10.77%</li>\n<li>Wonder Woman 5.87%</li>\n</ul>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/aquaman-10-e1623414326456.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-676019\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/aquaman-10-e1623414326456-700x299.jpg\" alt=\"aquaman 2 title\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/aquaman-10-e1623414326456-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/aquaman-10-e1623414326456-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/aquaman-10-e1623414326456-768x328.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/aquaman-10-e1623414326456.jpg 960w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2 dir=\"auto\"><strong>Do You Dare Disagree With the Mighty Survey Monkey?</strong></h2>\n<p>I don&#8217;t really have any qualms with this list. I mean, I don&#8217;t <em>agree</em> with it, and it&#8217;s immediately flawed because it omits three movies, but hey, I&#8217;m not going to get all bent out of shape. If I were ranking such a list, I&#8217;d probably say that <em>Suicide Squad</em> (which, again, isn&#8217;t even part of this survey) should be at the top – and therefore classified as the &#8220;worst DCEU movie.&#8221; Because&#8230;c&#8217;mon, it&#8217;s awful.</p>\n<p><em>Wonder Woman 1984</em> would be next, then <em>Batman v Superman</em>, then <em>Justice League</em>, then <strong><em>Man of Steel</em></strong>, followed by <em>Zack Snyder&#8217;s Justice League</em>. <em>Shazam!</em> and <em>Birds of Prey</em> (which also aren&#8217;t even on here, you stupid Survey Monkey) would be next, probably tied, followed by <strong><em>Wonder Woman</em></strong>, with <strong><em>Aquaman</em></strong> at the bottom – meaning <em>Aquaman</em> would be the best entry in the DCEU.</p>\n<p>I know that&#8217;s a controversial claim for many, but I firmly believe <em>Aquaman</em> is the best DCEU movie. Why? Because it understands how to have fun. <em>Aquaman</em> is inventive, and strange, and funny, and features an octopus playing drums. If you can&#8217;t get behind that, well, I don&#8217;t know what to tell you, kids.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/worst-dceu-movie/\">What is the Worst DCEU Movie? 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"Warner Bros. Really Wanted James Gunn to Make a Superman Movie Before He Chose ‘The Suicide Squad’","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683691","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/james-gunn-superman.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683727\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/james-gunn-superman-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"james gunn superman\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/james-gunn-superman-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/james-gunn-superman-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/james-gunn-superman-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/james-gunn-superman.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>James Gunn</strong> has made the leap from Marvel to DC with the upcoming <strong><em>The Suicide Squad</em></strong>, but we could&#8217;ve gotten a completely different DC movie from him if things had worked out differently. In a recent interview, Gunn confirmed that after he was fired by Disney and Marvel over offensive past tweets, Warner Bros. approached him and asked if he&#8217;d be interested in directing a new <strong><em>Superman</em></strong> movie. Gunn turned the offer down and eventually decided on <em>The Suicide Squad</em> instead. And based on Gunn&#8217;s sensibilities, that&#8217;s probably for the best.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683691\"></span></p>\n<p>In a new interview with the <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/07/14/movies/james-gunn-the-suicide-squad.html\">New York Times</a>, James Gunn reveals that after Marvel gave him the boot for offensive tweets, Warner Bros. came calling – and asked if he wanted to helm a new Superman movie. &#8220;They proposed that to me,&#8221; Gunn says. &#8220;Toby Emmerich [the Warner Bros. Pictures Group chairman], he works out with my manager, and every morning he would say, &#8216;James Gunn, Superman. James Gunn, Superman.'&#8221; Of course, we know that Gunn didn&#8217;t take the gig – he ended up picking <em>The Suicide Squad</em> instead.</p>\n<p>&#8220;At that time I said I can’t commit myself to something right now,&#8221; Gunn says. &#8220;It was traumatic. I had to deal with myself. I just have to take a step back. So I took the different possibilities of projects I could work on, and for a month, every day I worked on a different project. I really wanted to make sure that whatever I was going to write was going to be a great story, and if it worked out and I felt like directing it, I could. <em>Suicide Squad</em> was just the one that came to life immediately.&#8221;</p>\n<p>In the end, Gunn was able to have the best of both worlds, because not only did he get to direct <em>The Suicide Squad</em> for Warner Bros., but Disney and Marvel eventually came to their senses and re-hired him to come back for <em>Guardians of the Galaxy Vol. 3</em>. But <em>The Suicide Squad </em>came first.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I really loved [the original comic book writer] John Ostrander’s take, which was taking these Z-grade villains and throwing them into black-ops situations where they were totally disposable and they wouldn’t come out alive,&#8221; Gunn says. &#8220;I loved <em>The Dirty Dozen</em> as a kid. It’s that same concept, mixed with a DC comic.&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Superman-reboot-Ta-Nehisi-Coates.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-659767\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Superman-reboot-Ta-Nehisi-Coates-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"Superman reboot Ta-Nehisi Coates\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Superman-reboot-Ta-Nehisi-Coates-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Superman-reboot-Ta-Nehisi-Coates-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Superman-reboot-Ta-Nehisi-Coates-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Superman-reboot-Ta-Nehisi-Coates.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>The Future of Superman</strong></h2>\n<p>I really enjoy James Gunn&#8217;s work, but I also think he made the right call here. While Gunn is capable of sweetness with his work, he also has a built-in cynicism and off-kilter style that I don&#8217;t think would lend itself to Superman. As for what happens next for Supes, Warner Bros. is currently working with <strong>J.J. Abrams</strong> and writer <strong>Ta-Nehisi Coates</strong> on a <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/superman-reboot-ta-nehisi-coates/\">new <em>Superman</em> movie</a> that will have a Black actor playing the Man of Steel.</p>\n<p>Some have assumed this means Henry Cavill&#8217;s days of playing Superman are over, but it&#8217;s still unclear if that&#8217;s accurate. Sources have said that the Abrams/Coates Superman is going to be outside the DCEU continuity, similar to both <em>Joker</em> and the upcoming <em>The Batman</em>. Which means that if they wanted to bring Cavill&#8217;s Superman back, they could. For now, though, everything remains up in the air – much like Superman himself.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/james-gunn-superman/\">Warner Bros. Really Wanted James Gunn to Make a Superman Movie Before He Chose &#8216;The Suicide Squad&#8217;</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"‘Blue Bayou’ Trailer: Justin Chon’s Latest Film Promises to be Both Intimate and Timely","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683570","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683641\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/blue-bayou-e1626266328589-700x299.jpg\" alt=\"blue bayou trailer\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/blue-bayou-e1626266328589-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/blue-bayou-e1626266328589-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/blue-bayou-e1626266328589-768x328.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/blue-bayou-e1626266328589.jpg 1332w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Award-winning filmmaker <strong>Justin Chon</strong> gave audiences all the feels at Cannes with his latest film, <em><strong>Blue Bayou</strong></em>. Set against the rugged backdrop of southern Louisiana, <em>Blue Bayou</em> chronicles one family&#8217;s desperate attempt to stay together despite harsh immigration policies threatening to tear them apart.</p>\n<p>Have a tissue ready for the official <em>Blue Bayou</em> trailer below.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683570\"></span></p>\n<h2>Blue Bayou Trailer</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/Jh59H_d19Kg?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>This story looks precious and heartbreaking. As an unfortunate cynic, I actually do enjoy drama films about familial love. Even though I consider <em>Poltergeist</em> to fall under this category, there is clearly a timely relevance and seriousness with<em> Blue Bayou</em>. I also love how layered Cho&#8217;s character is and how the film seems to explore Asian American identity. &#8220;Where are you <em>really</em> from&#8221; is an often uncomfortable and ignorant question that many people experience in our melting pot of a country so it&#8217;s nice to see that written into the script.</p>\n<p>Focus Features describes <em>Blue Bayou</em> as &#8220;the moving and timely story of a uniquely American family fighting for their future. Antonio LeBlanc (<strong>Chon</strong>), a Korean adoptee raised in a small town in the Louisiana <span class=\"il\">bayou</span>, is married to the love of his life Kathy (<strong>Alicia Vikander</strong>), and step-dad to their beloved daughter Jessie (<strong>Sydney Kowalske</strong>). Struggling to make a better life for his family, he must confront the ghosts of his past when he discovers that he could be deported from the only country he has ever called home.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The cinematography is also noteworthy because of how sunshine and shadows are all captured. The approach makes the scenes simultaneously weathered but hopeful. Cinematographers <strong>Ante Cheng</strong> and <strong>Matthew Chuang</strong>&#8216;s use of lighting capture a notion of hard work, grit, sweat, and dirt in a lot of these scenes. This style also compliments <strong>Linda Ronstadt</strong>&#8216;s song &#8220;Blue Bayou,&#8221; which is where the film gets its title. With lyrics like &#8220;Saving nickels, saving dimes, Working &#8217;til the sun don&#8217;t shine, Looking forward to happier times on Blue Bayou,&#8221; it seems like an apt choice.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-576833\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ms.-purple-e1568378001603-700x308.jpg\" alt=\"justin chon interview\" width=\"700\" height=\"308\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ms.-purple-e1568378001603-700x308.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ms.-purple-e1568378001603-360x158.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ms.-purple-e1568378001603-768x338.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ms.-purple-e1568378001603.jpg 1100w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Building Borders and Breaking Hearts</h2>\n<p>Immigrant stories are American stories. Over the past few years, there have been some films that challenge the notion of what it means to be American and have sparked conversations that should respectfully continue. Director Lee Isaac Chung&#8217;s Oscar-winning film <em>Minari</em> is a prime example of what constitutes an American story, or an American film. Justin Chon tackles these themes in his films like critically acclaimed films like <em>Gook</em>, <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/justin-chon-interview-ms-purple/\"><em>Ms. Purple</em></a>, and now <em>Blue Bayou</em>.</p>\n<p>There is an assortment of films that center around immigration, even in animated form with the lovable <em>Paddington</em>. There are also several films that depict what the American Dream looks like as well as stories of American families. However, <em>Blue Bayou</em> seems to potentially stand out because it is a feature film that specifically mentions ICE and the immigration reform that has devastated so many American families. In addition to examining American identity and culture, it appears as though Chon&#8217;s latest film is a heartfelt effort to portray a problematic and divisive topic through an empathetic lens.</p>\n<p><em>Blue Bayou</em> will be released only in theaters on <strong>September 17th, 2021</strong></p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/blue-bayou-trailer-justin-chon/\">&#8216;Blue Bayou&#8217; Trailer: Justin Chon&#8217;s Latest Film Promises to be Both Intimate and Timely</a> appeared first on <a and everything else you could possibly stand to know.)</em></p>\n<p><strong>Kenneth Branagh</strong>&#8216;s attempt to create an entire film series around Agatha Christie&#8217;s Hercule Poirot continues with <strong><em>Death on the Nile</em></strong>, a movie that has already had its release date rescheduled multiple times. And the way things are going for some of the cast members, it might just get rescheduled again. For now, though, <em>Death on the Nile</em> is set for 2022, and I went ahead and rounded up what you need to know in advance.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683472\"></span></p>\n<h2><strong>Death on the Nile Release Date and Where You Can Watch It</strong></h2>\n<p><em>Death on the Nile</em> is currently scheduled to open on <strong>February 11, 2022</strong>. That could always change – it&#8217;s changed several times already, after all. For now, the film is a theatrical release. However, since this is owned by Disney, the studio could always decide to drop it onto Disney+. They could also attempt to release it in both theaters and on Disney+ with Premiere Access. As of the writing of this story, though, <em>Death on the Nile</em> is destined for theaters.</p>\n<h2><strong>What is </strong><strong>Death on the Nile</strong><strong>?</strong></h2>\n<p><em>Death on the Nile</em> is the follow-up to 2017&#8217;s <em>Murder on the Orient Express</em>. Calling it a sequel seems wrong, but it&#8217;s yet another story about Belgian detective Hercule Poirot trying to solve a murder with a cavalcade of suspects. The film is based on the Agatha Christie novel of the same name – a novel that&#8217;s been adapted several times before already, including a 1978 feature film starring Peter Ustinov.</p>\n<h2><strong>Death on the Nile Synopsis</strong></h2>\n<p>Here&#8217;s the <em>Death on the Nile</em> synopsis:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Belgian sleuth Hercule Poirot’s Egyptian vacation aboard a glamorous river steamer turns into a terrifying search for a murderer when a picture-perfect couple’s idyllic honeymoon is tragically cut short. Set against an epic landscape of sweeping desert vistas and the majestic Giza pyramids, this tale of unbridled passion and incapacitating jealousy features a cosmopolitan group of impeccably dressed travelers, and enough wicked twists and turns to leave audiences guessing until the final, shocking denouement.</p></blockquote>\n<h2><strong>Death on the Nile Director, Crew, and More</strong></h2>\n<p>Kenneth Branagh directs <em>Death on the Nile</em>, just as he did with <em>Murder on the Orient Express</em>. <strong>Michael Green</strong> penned the script. Producers include Ridley Scott, Mark Gordon, Simon Kinberg, Kenneth Branagh, Judy Hofflund, and Kevin J. Walsh, with Matthew Jenkins, James Prichard, and Matthew Prichard serving as executive producers. Haris Zambarloukos, who shot <em>Murder on the Orient Express</em>, is the cinematographer. Patrick Doyle handles the musical score.</p>\n<h2><strong>Death on the Nile Cast</strong></h2>\n<p>Kenneth Branagh and his mustache return as Hercule Poirot, leading a cast that includes<strong> Tom Bateman</strong>,<strong> Annette Bening</strong>, <strong>Russell Brand</strong>,<strong> Ali Fazal</strong>, <strong>Dawn French</strong>, <strong>Gal Gadot</strong>, <strong>Armie Hammer</strong>, <strong>Rose Leslie</strong>, <strong>Emma Mackey</strong>, <strong>Sophie Okonedo</strong>, <strong>Jennifer Saunders</strong>, and <strong>Letitia Wright</strong>.</p>\n<h2><strong>Death on the Nile 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"How the ‘Loki’ and ‘WandaVision’ Finales Set the Stage for the Next Phase of the MCU","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683664","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683708 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-wandavision-finale-combo-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"WandaVision, Loki and the Future of the MCU\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-wandavision-finale-combo.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-wandavision-finale-combo-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Even though Marvel Studios was forced to take a break from the big screen due to the coronavirus pandemic, it allowed the comic book movie studio to make waves with their new original shows on Disney+. It&#8217;s almost a blessing in disguise that Marvel&#8217;s movies were pushed back, allowing <strong><em>WandaVision</em></strong>, <strong><em>The Falcon and The Winter Soldier</em></strong>, and <strong><em>Loki</em></strong> to shine. In fact, the finales of both <em>WandaVision</em> and <em>Loki</em> have set the stage for a huge even that will have repercussions across the entire next phase of the MCU.<span id=\"more-683664\"></span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683711 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-hewhoremains-desk-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Loki - He Who Remains\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-hewhoremains-desk.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-hewhoremains-desk-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>The Loki Finale</h2>\n<p>Before we get into the nitty gritty of how the events of <em>Loki</em> and <em>WandaVision</em> will impact the larger Marvel Cinematic Universe, let&#8217;s dig into the <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-finale-review/\">finale of <em>Loki</em></a> a little bit.</p>\n<p>When Loki (<strong>Tom Hiddleston</strong>) and Sylvie (<strong>Sophia Di Martino</strong>) reach the end of time, they meet a character referred to by Miss Minutes as He Who Remains, and he&#8217;s played by <strong>Jonathan Majors</strong>. This realization seems to confirm the theories about Kang the Conqueror being behind the Time Variance Authority since Jonathan Majors has already been reported to play Kang the Conqueror in <em>Ant-Man and The Wasp: Quantumania</em>. But it also debunks them in a way.</p>\n<p>He Who Remains is really <a href=\"https://marvel.fandom.com/wiki/He_Who_Remains_(Multiverse)\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">an entirely different character</a> in Marvel Comics. Not only is he the creator of the Time Keepers, but he&#8217;s also the final director the TVA in the Citadel at the End of Time, which is the last remaining reality of the multiverse. However, it seems that label has now been applied to Kang the Conqueror.<em> Loki</em> gives us a version of He Who Remains, who is a variant of Kang. Though the name is never uttered, the &#8220;conqueror&#8221; label is briefly mentioned.</p>\n<p>Furthermore, He Who Remains warns that his death and the creation of the multiverse will bring about multiple variants of himself. Since Kang the Conqueror is known for conquering timelines, it&#8217;s safe to assume that all of his variants will be creating trouble across the multiverse. But besides that, the mere creation of the multiverse will pave the way for what&#8217;s to come in the rest of the Marvel Cinematic Universe.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-582322 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-farfromhome-panic-endcredits-700x294.jpg\" alt=\"Spider-Man: Far From Home Honest Trailer\" width=\"700\" height=\"294\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-farfromhome-panic-endcredits-700x294.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-farfromhome-panic-endcredits-360x151.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-farfromhome-panic-endcredits-768x323.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-farfromhome-panic-endcredits.jpg 962w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Spider-Man: No Way Home</h2>\n<p><em>Loki</em> has officially paved the way for the multiverse to break open in the Marvel Cinematic Universe, and it looks like the <em>Spider-Man</em> franchise will be the first Marvel Studios movie to feel the aftermath.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;ve been hearing for awhile now that <strong><em>Spider-Man: No Way Home</em></strong> will tap into the multiverse by not only bringing in multiple versions of Spider-Man with the return of Tobey Maguire and Andrew Garfield from their respective franchises (<a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/spider-man-3-tobey-maguire-andrew-garfield/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">despite denials of such a concept</a>), but also the return of villains like Doc Ock (<strong>Alfred Molina</strong>) and Electro (<strong>Jamie Foxx</strong>), from what we can now assume will be branded as alternate universes/timelines created by the death of He Who Remains.</p>\n<p>In <em>Spider-Man: No Way Home</em>, we&#8217;ve heard that Peter Parker (<strong>Tom Holland</strong>) seeks refuge in the Sanctum Sanctorum with Doctor Strange after his secret identity was revealed by J. Jonah Jameson (<strong>J.K. Simmons</strong>) via Mysterio (<strong>Jake Gyllenhaal</strong>). Joining him are MJ (<strong>Zendaya</strong>) and Ned (<strong>Jacob Batalon</strong>), who have been labeled as Spider-Man&#8217;s accomplices. Without getting into specifics until a trailer is officially revealed, it has been said that Peter Parker stumbles upon something in the Sanctum Sanctorum that will put him on a path to discovering the effects of the multiverse that was only previously teased as a lie told by Mysterio.</p>\n<p><em>Spider-Man: No Way Home</em> arrives on <strong>December 17, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-548519 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Road-to-Endgame-Doctor-Strange-3-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Road-to-Endgame-Doctor-Strange-3.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Road-to-Endgame-Doctor-Strange-3-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness</h2>\n<p>Since Doctor Strange (<strong>Benedict Cumerbatch</strong>) will be part of <em>Spider-Man: No Way Home</em>, we&#8217;re assuming the events of the webslinger&#8217;s sequel will also plant the seeds for whats to come in <strong><em>Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness</em></strong>. Though what unfolds in <em>No Way Home</em> will clearly be focused on how the multiverse impacts Peter Parker, the events of that movie will likely signal a bigger problem that Doctor Strange will have to deal with in his own sequel. And the presence of <strong>Elizabeth Olsen</strong> as Scarlet Witch in that movie may give us an idea of what one of those problems could be.</p>\n<p>At the end of <em>WandaVision</em>, a credits scene (which was <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wandavision-credits-scene-updated/\">mysteriously updated recently</a>) showed us Wanda Maximoff living in a cabin deep in the mountains. However, she wasn&#8217;t just enjoying a much needed getaway. Though Wanda was seen getting ready to enjoy a cup of tea, she was also seen in the form of an astral projection of the Scarlet Witch, reading through the Darkhold book of spells that will help enhance and grow her powerful magical and mystical abilities. But while Scarlet Witch was reading through the Darkhold, she was interrupted by echoes of her children yelling for help. That&#8217;s especially interesting since it was believed that her twin sons <span class=\"ILfuVd\"><span class=\"hgKElc\">Billy and Tommy</span></span> were only manifestations of her own magic within The Hex.</p>\n<p>Since Elizabeth Olsen has been reported to be a major player in <em>Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness</em>, we&#8217;re betting a major plot point will be Scarlet Witch trying to track down her kids in another universe. Could a variant of Kang the Conqueror be responsible for holding her kids captive in another universe? Will that be something that triggers the madness of the multiverse, or is it just part of the larger debacle that Doctor Strange is trying to deal with?</p>\n<p><em>Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness</em> is slated for release on <strong>March 25, 2022</strong>.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-481471 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/antmanandthewasp-trailerbreakdown-antman-wasp-facing-700x288.jpg\" alt=\"Ant-Man and the Wasp Box Office\" width=\"700\" height=\"288\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/antmanandthewasp-trailerbreakdown-antman-wasp-facing-700x288.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/antmanandthewasp-trailerbreakdown-antman-wasp-facing-360x148.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/antmanandthewasp-trailerbreakdown-antman-wasp-facing-768x316.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/antmanandthewasp-trailerbreakdown-antman-wasp-facing.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Ant-Man and The Wasp: Quantumania</h2>\n<p>Well, now that we&#8217;ve met one version of Kang the Conqueror in the <em>Loki</em> finale, it only makes sense that we&#8217;ll meet a variant of him in the upcoming third installment of the <strong><em>Ant-Man</em></strong> franchise. We&#8217;re not entirely sure what to expect from this one, but there is one detail from <em>Ant-Man and The Wasp</em> that will likely be a key component of the villain&#8217;s presence in this sequel.</p>\n<p>In <em>Ant-Man and The Wasp</em>, when Janet Van Dyne (<strong>Michelle Pfeiffer</strong>) is rescued from the Quantum Realm by Hank Pym (<strong>Michael Douglas</strong>), <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/quantum-realm-mcu/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">you can see an entire city in the background</a>, implying that there&#8217;s a whole civilization in this subatomic world. Could a version of Kang the Conqueror be stuck there? Perhaps he&#8217;s been working on a way to escape, and after being left behind by Janet Van Dyne, maybe he&#8217;s pissed and wants to take it out on the rest of the world.</p>\n<p>Jonathan Majors <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/ant-man-3-villain/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">was already cast</a> as Kang the Conqueror in<em> Ant-Man and The Wasp: Quantumania</em> before <em>Loki</em> premiered, which is why so many theories about the character popping up in the show manifested themselves after the very first episode. What will this version of Kang the Conqueror bring to the table?</p>\n<p><em>Ant-Man and The Wasp</em> is slated to arrive in theaters on <strong>February 17, 2023</strong>.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683709 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-multiverse-tvascreen-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Loki - TVA Multiverse Screen\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-multiverse-tvascreen.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-multiverse-tvascreen-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Loki and The Future of the MCU</h2>\n<p>Now that his presence in the MCU has been confirmed, along with plenty of variants across the multiverse, there are endless possibilities for how the villain will have an impact on the next phase of the MCU, and that&#8217;s exactly what <em>Loki</em> head writer <strong>Michael Waldron</strong> intended.</p>\n<p>Before <em>Loki</em> even premiered, head writer Michael Waldron <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-mcu-ramifications-michael-waldron/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">teased major ramifications</a> for the Marvel Cinematic Universe. Now he&#8217;s confirmed how Kang the Conqueror fulfills that threat in a conversation with <a href=\"https://www.marvel.com/articles/tv-shows/loki-he-who-remains-jonathan-majors\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Marvel.com</a>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;We knew that we wanted this show to be huge, and we wanted it to really end with a bang and have a huge impact on the MCU moving forward. Knowing that Kang was probably going to be the next big cross-movie villain, and because he is a time-traveling, multiversal adversary, it just always made so much sense. I came up with that big multiversal war mythology and pitched it out in the room one day to our producers. And they said, yeah, let&#8217;s go for it. We knew we were going to end up meeting the man behind the curtain. And then it was just on us to make sure that that meeting really delivered.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>Does this make Kang the Conqueror the new Thanos? The villain started out as a looming threat in a credits scene from <em>The Avengers</em>, but the full breadth of his threat wouldn&#8217;t be felt until <em>Avengers: Infinity War</em>. Could we see multiple versions of Kang the Conqueror coming together as the next major threat for the entire MCU? That seems possible with how Waldron intentionally teased what&#8217;s to come. The writer said:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;You had to leave a lot of meat on the bone in terms of how evil he could be, because that&#8217;s He Who Remains&#8217; whole thing, that it&#8217;s not me who you should be afraid of. ‘It&#8217;s the other versions of me that are going to come.’ It was trying to really hint at that terrifying evil within without going all the way there.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>So instead of giving us a full-on villain, Waldron gave us a version of Kang the Conqueror who was at the end of his rope, tired of ruling over time. But he still wrote the character as a &#8220;very charismatic sociopath,&#8221; hinting at the madness that any of his variants could bring. Imagine how crazy and deadly a version of Kang the Conqueror could be when he&#8217;s not sick of living for eons.</p>\n<p>On a side note, the introduction of the multiverse in this fashion is an interesting way to retroactively make every Marvel movie or TV show every made part of the Marvel Cinematic Universe. Perhaps that&#8217;s why Marvel&#8217;s <em>What If&#8230;?</em> animated series <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/what-if-ties-to-the-mcu/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">may have more significant ties</a> to the MCU than we&#8217;re expecting. Maybe this is how we&#8217;ll get Tom Holland&#8217;s Spider-Man to meet Tom Hardy&#8217;s Venom or even the introduction of the X-Men and Fantastic Four. Literally anything is possible.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wandavision-loki-and-the-future-of-the-mcu/\">How the &#8216;Loki&#8217; and &#8216;WandaVision&#8217; Finales Set the Stage for the Next Phase of the MCU</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Anderton","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-wandavision-finale-combo-700x300.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn39@2020_4/2021/07/14/17-33-45-229_0b87cda4aa4d2462.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-hewhoremains-desk-700x300.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn23@2020_1/2021/07/14/17-33-46-758_1f9c7160ef318fd5.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/spiderman-farfromhome-panic-endcredits-700x294.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn55@2020_5/2021/07/14/17-33-47-058_558cd019f0b05668.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Road-to-Endgame-Doctor-Strange-3-700x300.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn47@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-33-47-464_acf786d11af76fd3.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/antmanandthewasp-trailerbreakdown-antman-wasp-facing-700x288.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn32@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-33-46-379_08b676b2a36f09e1.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-multiverse-tvascreen-700x300.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn79@2020_5/2021/07/14/17-33-46-226_448fc79ff0927c1c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn40@2020_4/2021/07/14/17-33-46-881_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=2OrUTQeMY4w:cprhtJDHGQs:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn87@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-33-47-114_809ba1123123f42a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn92@2020_6/2021/07/14/17-33-47-600_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=2OrUTQeMY4w:cprhtJDHGQs:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn36@2020_1/2021/07/14/17-33-45-941_5d6d8df9d3406a1a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/2OrUTQeMY4w":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn35@2020_5/2021/07/14/17-33-58-908_b213a61fed77a777.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626284004433},{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"‘Gunpowder Milkshake’ Director Navot Papushado on Taking Inspiration From Jackie Chan and Buster Keaton [Interview]","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=681364","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-676739\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Gunpowder-Milkshake-Trailer-New-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"Gunpowder Milkshake Trailer New\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Gunpowder-Milkshake-Trailer-New-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Gunpowder-Milkshake-Trailer-New-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Gunpowder-Milkshake-Trailer-New-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Gunpowder-Milkshake-Trailer-New.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><em><strong>Gunpowder Milkshake </strong></em>is a movie that lives up to its title. For starters, it looks like sugar, with its candy-like aesthetic – it&#8217;s a visual treat from director <strong>Navot Papushado</strong> and one of the all-time great cinematographers, <strong>Michael Seresin</strong>. Seresin shot several of filmmaker Alan Parker&#8217;s films, including <em>Angel Heart</em>, <em>Midnight Express</em>, and the joyous <em>Bugsy Malone</em>. To say Papushado was excited to work with him is an understatement. But I&#8217;m getting ahead of myself.</p>\n<p>Papushado made an impression with his 2013 film, <em>Big Bad Wolves</em>, which Quentin Tarantino called <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/quentin-tarantino-calls-israeli-thriller-big-bad-wolves-the-best-film-of-the-year/\">the best film</a> of that year. Since then, Paushado shot a segment for the horror anthology <em>ABCs of Death 2</em>, but after a long wait, he got back behind the camera for this original but extremely referential action movie starring<strong> Karen Gillan</strong> and <strong>Lena Headey</strong>, among others (read our review <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/gunpowder-milkshake-review/\">here</a>).</p>\n<p>During our interview ahead of the film&#8217;s release on Netflix today, the filmmaker shared a long list of influences in his action-packed genre blender.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-681364\"></span></p>\n<p><strong>You have obviously one of the greatest cinematographers around shooting this movie. Did you two ever talk about<em> Bugsy Malone</em>? That feels like an influence.</strong></p>\n<p>I think we left that unspoken. We didn&#8217;t want to touch that stuff. No, I grew up on<em> Bugsy Malone</em>, and I think I grew up on that duo, Michael Seresin and Alan Parker, before I even understood there are people who are actually making those movies. For me, movies magically appeared in a cinema or on TV.</p>\n<p>I had video cassettes of <em>Bugsy Malone</em>, <em>Birdie</em>, and <em>Angel&#8217;s Heart</em>. I was a big fan of Michael Seresin before I even made the connection there&#8217;s a camera or the DOP behind it. So when hearing Michael Seresin might be available, I was like, &#8220;All right. Everyone knows their job. Everyone knows what to do.&#8221; And then he read it. He was living just two blocks from where I was living back then. And he&#8217;s like, &#8220;Hey, yeah, why don&#8217;t you come over for dinner? We&#8217;ll open a bottle of wine and talk about our influences and discuss the script?&#8221;</p>\n<p>I went there, and we just spent a wonderful day. And then the next day, we met again, and we just realized we loved the same movies, some of his, but many others more. And the approach I wanted to bring to this movie was exactly what he represents. It&#8217;s this understanding of the rich history of film, the mythology behind all the movies that I adore and love, which is pretty much some of his favorites. We wanted to see if we can bring it into something modern and contemporary and do the whole movie wide lenses, very colorful, something that is almost been done on a Technicolor era of, maybe it&#8217;s a <em>Vertigo</em>. What would have happened if Hitchcock [did this]?</p>\n<p>I apologize for trying to put me and him in the same sentence. It&#8217;s just for demonstrating my ambitiousness. And yeah, Michael, I learned so much from him. I&#8217;m very lucky to call him a friend. I was just on the phone with him a couple of hours ago. He&#8217;s shooting the new Noah Baumbach movie, and he&#8217;s very excited about that. He&#8217;s a legend.</p>\n<p><strong>What were some of the other movies you two talked about? </strong></p>\n<p>It always starts with this holy trinity of three filmmakers I adore and keep watching their moves again and again, and it&#8217;s Alfred Hitchcock, Akira Kurosawa, and Sergio Leone. For me, it all starts there and especially when you discuss the assassin genre. It goes all the way back to the gunslingers and the contract killers and the hired hitmen. And then it evolves into what Jean-Pierre Melville introduced. And from John-Pierre Melville, let&#8217;s stay a little bit in the French cinema.</p>\n<p>Jacques Denys is someone I adore. So, we say, &#8220;Okay, wouldn&#8217;t it be great if we incorporate those Technicolors, those <em>Umbrellas of Cherbourg</em>, <em>Singing In the Rain</em>, into an Alfred Hitchcock, Sergio Leone kind of genre blender?&#8221;And then we discussed a little bit later on, the Michael Mann and Michael Cimino effect that on the &#8217;70s and Frankenheimer, Friedkin, and Scorsese. And being an &#8217;80s kid, I was born into the Spielberg-Zemeckis era.</p>\n<p>So I felt like this is who I am. This is what I want to bring in. I think those filmmakers were also influenced by the same eras that I was. So it became very clear that we want to do something colorful, super stylish, very meticulous, wide lenses, dim lights, almost give it a nostalgic, retro-chic, but without holding the contemporary or the kind of modern aspect of it, so it wouldn&#8217;t feel like we are indulging our own kind of, &#8220;Oh, we want to show you all the movies we like.&#8221;</p>\n<p>No, we wanted them to be there, in the presence and in spirit. We wanted to do justice to all the rich mythology, all the names we mentioned. I always felt like that when you&#8217;re doing a movie in a specific genre, you have to acknowledge and respect everything that came before you, try not to copy too much, but at least acknowledge that.</p>\n<p><strong>Let&#8217;s talk about the action, starting with the hospital fight sequence, which gives the character such a fun challenge to overcome. With the stunt team, how did you want to incorporate physical comedy into that fight? </strong></p>\n<p>For me, the two best action heroes are Buster Keaton and Jackie Chan. Their action sequences are funny, but more than anything else, they provoke emotion through storytelling. For them, it&#8217;s all about either the plot moving forward or the character&#8217;s arc. It&#8217;s never about nihilistic, shoot-em-up kind of a thing.</p>\n<p>I&#8217;m also a big fan of Asian cinema and Korean cinema and Japanese and Chinese and everything. In those movies, guns play a part, but it&#8217;s actually the challenges that you throw on your characters. It&#8217;s also a challenge on yourself as a writer, how can I push my heroine into the most difficult, absurd surrealist situation and see how she can come up or recover from that?</p>\n<p>Now, having said that, those action scenes were written the way that they are. But once the entire [stunt] team came on board, they kept pushing the envelope. They would come to me, and they would say, &#8220;Listen, Karen is good. Lena is good. We can push it a little bit more. How about this and about that?&#8221; And then Michelle joined in, then Angela joined in, and then Carl joined in. Okay, we needed to rethink it a little bit. We need to create more challenges for ourselves. I&#8217;m not going to put just two guns at Michelle&#8217;s hand. I mean, she jumped on a moving train with the bike. I can come up with something a little bit more creative. So, a chain would be more fitting, that will challenge us and her a little bit.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-644877\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/gunpowder-milkshake-1-700x312.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"312\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/gunpowder-milkshake-1-700x312.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/gunpowder-milkshake-1-360x160.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/gunpowder-milkshake-1-768x342.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>But from the beginning, it was always about the storytelling. And for me, the clinic fight also kind of represented little evolutionary step that the movie takes, from something that is more Jackie Chan, Buster Keaton-oriented, like the bowling alley fight, into the more cartoonish kind of Looney Tunes, Chuck Jones meets <em>Who Framed Roger Rabbit?</em> And later on, you have the car chase, which is more of a &#8217;70s kind of a thing. And later on, you have more of a <em>Wild Bunch</em>, Sam Peckinpah, let&#8217;s go down in a blaze of glory. This is where we make our stand.</p>\n<p>So we tried to keep engaging with ourselves, with our characters, and also with the audience, with fresh new takes on, okay, not just another thing of what you already got used to seeing. No, let&#8217;s try to confuse you and dazzle you and then play with you. I always love to make the audience part of the movie, not just a spectator, keep guessing. So, she&#8217;s got her hands paralyzed. Hmm. I wonder what you&#8217;re going to do now.</p>\n<p><strong>The car chase is another good example of that. It&#8217;s big but in a small location. </strong></p>\n<p>Exactly. It was written like that. I think most of the car chases are being done with the budget of our entire movie. Now, what if you go smaller? And by going smaller, by giving yourself more restrictions, by thinking more confined, you actually come up with something that feels not only bigger but much more entertaining.</p>\n<p>I was wanting to kind of make my little homage to <em>Bullitt</em>, to <em>The French Connection</em>, but given them my own little take. How would that kind of a car chase be translated into something narrow and small and confined and how to make it cat and mouse, kind of a thing?</p>\n<p><strong>The ending is where you go big. What was challenging about putting all those moving pieces together? </strong></p>\n<p>That was a challenge. I remember Michelle, I think she was flying from<em> Avatar</em>, and she just came for one day, for fitting, for seeing the action. We were all in awe, because it&#8217;s Michelle Yeoh, coming to the training stage. It took everyone else a week or two. She just comes in and very elegantly, just nails everything. We were all like, &#8220;Yeah, that&#8217;s Michelle Yeoh.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Everything that comes to play in the action to do with the colors, the location that was firstly designed by our production designer and by Michael Seresin, but also with the costume designer, <strong>Louise Frogley</strong>, which did an incredible job, I think. We wanted them to be practical, professional, but still stylish. Like, this is their territory. This is their turf. So it&#8217;s a lot of moving parts. But if you have the most amazing team and the most amazing cast, you just need to make sure you don&#8217;t screw it up, I guess.</p>\n<p><strong>Having said all that, it&#8217;s a close-up of Michelle Yeoh&#8217;s face that, to me, is the high point. </strong></p>\n<p>She&#8217;s an icon. I think all these ladies are iconic. And yes, you have Michelle Yeoh in this one shot, which I think is a very also emotional moment. Like I said, most of the movie was shot with these wide lenses. For certain moments, we really wanted to emphasize something, like where it was Carla&#8217;s moment, just before the last fight. Those moments where we savor them. We wanted to savor them. You don&#8217;t see them a lot. Because they&#8217;re happening at the very specific moment of the script, they have that impact on you.</p>\n<p><strong>How about the bowling alley fight? How was it timing that fight? </strong></p>\n<p>So we wanted to establish how badass she is, even before she starts fighting. So it&#8217;s all the build-up. It&#8217;s her standing there, and the three stooges, they&#8217;re far away from her, and they&#8217;re not even jumping at her. They&#8217;re almost like they&#8217;re prolonging the way. And you can just go at her, like 3, 2, 1. But by building and establishing the weight, you kind of like, all right, she&#8217;s a badass. And they&#8217;re a little bit intimidated and afraid, although she&#8217;s outnumbered and outgunned or out-weapon-ed.</p>\n<p><strong>She towers over them.</strong></p>\n<p>Yeah. She kind of plays with them. She&#8217;s like this little cat, knows these three mice are coming. She taunts them and humiliates them in a way that will come and haunt you later. But when the fight starts, we wanted to create the first part of it in one long take, to kind of demonstrate how badass she is and how capable she is. I think for Karen, maybe I&#8217;m wrong, but I think that was most challenging and rewarding because then that&#8217;s the thing we worked the hardest.</p>\n<p>In many ways, the clinic fight doesn&#8217;t require the same set of skills, is more of an acting kind of thing, because of the restrictions. But this was pure skills. Karen needed to be well versed in the ways of martial arts and kicking ass. It was a challenge because we wanted to show the choreography. So again, it&#8217;s this couple of things working together. It&#8217;s the wild lenses, the long take, them, and the neon. You can see them as a silhouette. As an audience, you would only be focused on the choreography, on how they come in and now they go out. It was so much fun.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\">***</p>\n<p><em>Gunpowder Milkshake</em> is now streaming on Netflix.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/gunpowder-milkshake-director-interview/\">&#8216;Gunpowder Milkshake&#8217; Director Navot Papushado on Taking Inspiration From Jackie Chan and Buster Keaton [Interview]</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a
