+0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Gunpowder-Milkshake-Trailer-New-700x321.jpg","linkMd5":"e20f7f523b2bfd509996945f0dda9448","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn14@2020_5/2021/07/14/17-33-39-140_78d89520d19ff7de.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":321,"sourceBytes":40225,"destBytes":25150,"author":"Jack Giroux","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Gunpowder-Milkshake-Trailer-New-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn14@2020_5/2021/07/14/17-33-39-140_78d89520d19ff7de.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/gunpowder-milkshake-1-700x312.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn31@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-33-58-936_ca2031e957a15872.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn40@2020_4/2021/07/14/17-33-46-881_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=dzGwcQxHQHg:dgvbKjP-eDI:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn52@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-33-46-572_cd7c0fd7971d0562.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn92@2020_6/2021/07/14/17-33-47-600_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=dzGwcQxHQHg:dgvbKjP-eDI:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn83@2020_5/2021/07/14/17-33-46-284_e526baf917f818d7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/dzGwcQxHQHg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn34@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-33-59-849_952924b3aa077293.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626284004433},{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"‘Titane’ Review: ‘Raw’ Director Julia Ducournau Returns With a Shocking Body-Horror Show [Cannes]","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683653","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683654\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/titane-e1626269617865-700x299.jpeg\" alt=\"titane review\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/titane-e1626269617865-700x300.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/titane-e1626269617865-360x154.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/titane-e1626269617865-768x328.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/titane-e1626269617865.jpeg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Julia Ducournau</strong> stunned Cannes audiences back in 2016 with <em>Raw</em>, the story of a vegetarian veterinarian student who soon develops a taste for manflesh. She returns in 2021 with <strong><em>Titane</em></strong>, an even more stylized, violent and resonant work set to shake up the main competition for Palme D’or.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683653\"></span></p>\n<p>The film begins in a car trip, with a haughty teen obnoxiously prodding the father in the front seat. After excoriating her to stop, she rebels, removing a seatbelt. A moment later the car smashes into a barrier, her head lacerated and requiring surgery to implement a titanium plate that gives the film its name. The result is a grisly scar on the side of her head, and a sense of rebellion and anger that is not soon quelled.</p>\n<p>We’re never sure on the gender of the character (we hear it’s a her only in surgery), and this gender fluidity will play a large role throughout the film. At the outset, however, it’s clear that Alexia is outwardly presenting as female, twerking and grinding at an auto show while vapid men circle to admire in order to get autographs. There’s a shower scene that follows that plays with the prison trope of a dropped bar of soap to tragicomic effect, her wild hair locked in the nipple piercing of her neighbor.</p>\n<p>This is one among many moments where the mix of pain and pleasure is at the fore, and it also speaks to the way the character themselves navigates their sullen and withdrawn air with an apparent need to surround themselves with companionship, if only briefly. Walking in the parking lot only to be chased by an admirer, the film again turns expectation, twisting the notion of a dame in distress on its head and thrusting us into the most brutal of altercations.</p>\n<p>Alexia returns to the car show to spend time alone with her flame-covered Cadillac. Naked and dripping with water from her post-rampage second shower, she straps herself in on the cadaverous-colored upholstered seats and quite literally is fucked by the automobile. David Cronenberg, whose divisive <em>Crash</em> won a special jury award in 1996 for &#8220;daring and audacity,&#8221; would hopefully be pleased that a new generation has taken up his kind of cinematic kink.</p>\n<p>The following is a series of murders and mayhem that showcase the true sociopathy of the central character, only to land, in both elegant and startling ways, into an almost sweet family drama with a father who has lost his son. Think of this as Ken Russell’s <em>Yentl</em> and you’ll see how two individuals can share a lie for mutual benefit. Set in a fire house, there literally are flames that erupt between the two, yet in each they manage to find something to make each other just a tiny bit more whole.</p>\n<p>The film soon doubled down on the body horror component, and it’s here that it all feels a bit underbaked. I for one didn’t need the long, grand, protracted reveal, and it’s frankly a bit superfluous and supernatural for what otherwise would have for me been an absolute gem. It’s this insistence to further one-up what was already confidently a weird and wild ride that makes it feel as if it’s gone off the rails, while certainly the gasps from the audience may indicate others will feel far differently. I could have lost the entire storyline that leads to the final scene and had a far more satisfying experience, but I may be in the minority on this one.</p>\n<p>At any rate, thanks to committed performances by Agathe Rousselle, Vincent Lindon, and the rest of the cast, there’s plenty to bite into on both the character and narrative level. The dynamic between the two individuals who essentially adopt each other brings out much of the film’s heart, and it’s extremely effective how it all plays out.</p>\n<p>Take a dash of Miike and Refn, a whole heap of Cronenberg and, above all, Ducournau’s uniquely acidic vision, and you have a unique cinematic alloy that does far more than rely upon shock and horror. It’s a film that’s at its best when things matter and you’re empathizing even during moments of total butchery. It’s never easy to inject humanity into inhumane acts, yet <em>Titane</em>, like the metal, manages to do something remarkably strong in a compact form. The film does excess without being excessive, drawing us into Alexia and Vincent’s tumultuous world and finding that the deepest connections are based on the lies we choose to share.</p>\n<p><strong>/Film Rating: 7.5 out of 10</strong></p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/titane-review-cannes/\">&#8216;Titane&#8217; Review: &#8216;Raw&#8217; Director Julia Ducournau Returns With a Shocking Body-Horror Show [Cannes]</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=Pw9nfzK0IgY:CjeGmy6IXhc:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=Pw9nfzK0IgY:CjeGmy6IXhc:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=Pw9nfzK0IgY:CjeGmy6IXhc:V_sGLiPBpWU\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=Pw9nfzK0IgY:CjeGmy6IXhc:I9og5sOYxJI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=Pw9nfzK0IgY:CjeGmy6IXhc:EGzC5_Ws_ZE\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=Pw9nfzK0IgY:CjeGmy6IXhc:EGzC5_Ws_ZE\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/Pw9nfzK0IgY\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 14 Jul 2021 13:49:23 +0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/titane-e1626269617865-700x299.jpeg","linkMd5":"aec0a18efa8a984a7002ab8a99f4d909","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn20@2020_6/2021/07/14/17-33-39-275_bf897afa3a5d3bfd.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":299,"sourceBytes":23077,"destBytes":14366,"author":"Jason Gorber","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/titane-e1626269617865-700x299.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn20@2020_6/2021/07/14/17-33-39-275_bf897afa3a5d3bfd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn40@2020_4/2021/07/14/17-33-46-881_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=Pw9nfzK0IgY:CjeGmy6IXhc:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn43@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-33-46-536_24ce8563a287de15.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn92@2020_6/2021/07/14/17-33-47-600_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=Pw9nfzK0IgY:CjeGmy6IXhc:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn99@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-33-46-882_ec5a839bf1610ba1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/Pw9nfzK0IgY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn31@2020_4/2021/07/14/17-33-47-244_0373a14ea4348ef5.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626284004433},{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"What is the Multiverse? Five Must-See Alternate Timeline TV Episodes to Watch After ‘Loki’","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683401","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-681281 size-medium\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/vfd5020_105_comp_v007_f5116a53-700x293.jpeg\" alt=\"multiverse tv episodes\" width=\"700\" height=\"293\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/vfd5020_105_comp_v007_f5116a53.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/vfd5020_105_comp_v007_f5116a53-360x151.jpeg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Look, I get it — multiverse storytelling can be confusing. Marvel&#8217;s <strong><em>Loki</em></strong> streaming series is only the latest in a long line of stories that plays fast and loose with the idea of multiple or parallel timelines. <em>Loki </em>follows the God of Mischief (<strong>Tom Hiddleston</strong>) after he gets involved with the Time Variance Authority, or the TVA, as they try to correct problems in individual timelines. This provides us a chance to see lots of variant Lokis (<a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/alligator-loki/\">including our favorite chompy green boy</a>) and opens up opportunities for a lot of zany storytelling that doesn&#8217;t necessarily have to impact the primary timeline.</p>\n<p>The idea of multiple universes existing at the same time isn&#8217;t anything new. Some of the earliest examples date back to Norse mythology, which divided existence into nine worlds. DC Comics first introduced the idea of the DC multiverse in its comics in <em>All Star Comics #3</em><strong> </strong>in 1940, and Marvel later followed suit, starting with their <strong><em>What if?</em></strong> series in the 1970s. While the concept of parallel universes might feel a little daunting to contemplate on your own, these five television episodes will help you understand the magic of the multiverse.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683401\"></span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683521 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/theparallel-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/theparallel.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/theparallel-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>&#8220;The Parallel&#8221; — The Twilight Zone</h2>\n<p>When it comes to television that changed the way we think, <strong>Rod Serling</strong>&#8216;s <em><strong>The Twilight Zone</strong></em><em> </em>is the forebear of them all. The original series ran from 1959 to 1964 and contained stories from science fiction greats like <strong>Ray Bradbury </strong>(<em><strong>Farhenheit 451</strong></em>) and  <strong>Richard Matheson </strong>(<em><strong>I Am Legend</strong></em>). Each episode in the anthology series told a different short story, most with the intent of exploring some political or social allegory.</p>\n<p>In 1963&#8217;s &#8220;The Parallel&#8221;, Major Robert Gaines (<strong>Steve Forrest</strong>) is orbiting earth in his space capsule when he suddenly blacks out and wakes up on Earth with no memory of how he got there. He&#8217;s uninjured, but the world he&#8217;s arrived in doesn&#8217;t quite match the one he left. His daughter suspects he&#8217;s someone else, his house suddenly has a white picket fence that his wife swears has always been there, and everyone keeps calling him Colonel, which matches his uniform but not his memories. He&#8217;s a little shaken until he comes to the conclusion that he&#8217;s in a parallel universe, and then takes steps to get back to his own timeline.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The Parallel&#8221; marks the first instance of multiverse storytelling on TV. It doesn&#8217;t do anything particularly groundbreaking and is a middle-of-the-road <em>The Twilight Zone</em> episode, but it&#8217;s the first, which means it paved the way for everyone else to tell TV stories about parallel universes and doppelgangers.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683524 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/startrekmirror-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/startrekmirror.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/startrekmirror-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>&#8220;Mirror Mirror&#8221;/&#8221;Crossover&#8221; — Star Trek/Star Trek Deep Space Nine</h2>\n<p>Did I say doppelgangers? If there&#8217;s one franchise that has capitalized on the potential fun of meeting your alternate self, it&#8217;s <em><strong>Star Trek</strong></em>. In the &#8220;Mirror Mirror&#8221; episode of the original series, a teleporter mishap sends Kirk, McCoy, Scotty, and Uhura to a parallel dimension where everything is reversed. The Federation has become an evil Empire, Kirk is a tyrant, and Spock has a goatee (that&#8217;s how you know he&#8217;s evil). The episode started several tropes about doppelgangers (including the whole goatee thing), and paved the way for future <em>Star Trek</em> iterations to really go wild with the Mirror Universe.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Star Trek: Deep Space Nine </strong></em>explored the Mirror Universe more than any other <em>Star Trek</em> series, with stories taking place there over five different episodes. The first of these, &#8220;Crossover,&#8221; is the most important and sets the stage for the later mirror episodes. In &#8220;Crossover,&#8221; Major Kira (<strong>Nana Visitor</strong>) and Doctor Bashir (<strong>Alexander Siddig</strong>) have an accident inside of the wormhole near the planet Bajor, sending them to the Mirror Universe. It&#8217;s been decades since Kirk and co. crossed over, but things are still pretty backwards in the Mirrorverse. Instead of the Federation, there&#8217;s a coalition between the Klingons, Cardassians, and Bajorans. Terrans (a fancy word for Earthlings) have been enslaved. The space station Deep Space Nine is instead a mining operation, run by the alternate Kira, the Intendant.</p>\n<p>There are few things in the world as enjoyable as watching Visitor play her double role. The entire cast really gets to go for it with their Mirrorverse personas, and you can tell they&#8217;re having a blast. The Mirror Universe in <em>Deep Space Nine</em> gave the actors a chance to explore their characters in new ways, and it provided more insight into their individual pathos. Sure, the Mirrorverse versions were the &#8220;evil&#8221; versions of themselves, but there were still versions of themselves. Kira is a strong leader with a dry sense of humor, regardless of whether she&#8217;s the former Bajoran freedom fighter or the Intendant. &#8220;Crossover&#8221; set up the following four <em>Deep Space Nine</em> Mirror episodes, including episodes where Captain Sisko (<strong>Avery Brooks</strong>) must pretend to be his doppelganger and deal with the fact that his dead wife is still very alive in the parallel universe. Some of the episodes are silly fun, and some are a bit more heady, but they all get to explore sides of these characters that we&#8217;ve never seen before.</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-683704 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/eviltroyandevilabed-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/eviltroyandevilabed.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/eviltroyandevilabed-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>&#8220;Remedial Chaos Theory&#8221; — Community</h2>\n<p>The NBC sitcom <em><strong>Community</strong></em> frequently made its own riffs on popular tropes, and it had an utter field day with parallel universes. In the season 3 episode, &#8220;Remedial Chaos Theory,&#8221; viewers are treated to seeing six different ways the same evening could have played out. The friends, who met in a Spanish study group at their community college, are all celebrating Troy (<strong>Donald Glover</strong>) and Abed (<strong>Danny Pudi</strong>) moving into a new apartment. When the pizza arrives, group leader Jeff (<strong>Joel McHale</strong>) suggests they roll dice to see who has to go get the pizza. Abed, who is sensitive to tropes, points out that Jeff is creating new timelines by introducing chance, and then we get to see each of them play out.</p>\n<p>What &#8220;Remedial Chaos Theory&#8221; does is brilliant. It&#8217;s a bottle episode, all set in one location with no visible impact on the overall plot. However, by seeing how the situations change each time a single character is removed from the group dynamic, we&#8217;re able to learn so much more about the group as a whole. The episode gives us insight into the characters and their relationships by changing up the formula just a pinch and removing one element. In the Darkest Timeline, which leaves Pierce (<strong>Chevy Chase</strong>) dead and severely maims the rest of the group, it&#8217;s revealed that things fall apart without Troy in the mix. At the end of the episode, the prime timeline continues and it&#8217;s Jeff who has to go get the pizza. This ends up being the most positive of the timelines, which means maybe the group is better off without Jeff at all. It&#8217;s a great piece of character storytelling and even ends with the Darkest Timeline versions of Troy and Abed making felt goatees for themselves before declaring they are Evil Troy and Evil Abed.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683527 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/rixtyminutes-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/rixtyminutes.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/rixtyminutes-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>&#8220;Rixty Minutes&#8221; &#8211; Rick and Morty</h2>\n<p><em>Community </em>showrunner <strong>Dan Harmon</strong> clearly has a love for stories involving parallel timelines, so it&#8217;s no surprise that he expanded on those ideas in <em><strong>Rick and Morty</strong></em>, the adult animated series he developed with <strong>Justin Roiland</strong>. <em>Rick and Morty</em> is a kind of <em><strong>Back to the Future</strong></em><em> </em>for twisted adults; it follows the adventures of alcoholic mad scientist Rick Sanchez (Roiland) and his hapless grandson Morty Smith (also Roiland) as they travel through space and time. In the first season episode &#8220;Rixty Minutes,&#8221; Rick introduces the entire Smith family to the many parallel timelines that exist. He and Morty watch Interdimensional Cable in the A plot, which gives Roiland a chance for lots of fun improvisational gags, but the B plot is more interesting. In order to enjoy his cable watching, Rick gives Morty&#8217;s parents and sister a helmet that will let them see through the eyes of some of their alternate selves.</p>\n<p>Jerry (<strong>Chris Parnell</strong>) finds a version of himself that&#8217;s a huge Hollywood player who parties with <strong>Johnny Depp</strong>. Beth (<strong>Sarah Chalke</strong>) finds a reality where she&#8217;s not a horse surgeon, but a human surgeon, like she always wanted. Their teenage daughter Summer (<strong>Spencer Grammar</strong>) discovers that she was an unplanned pregnancy and that her parents argued about whether or not to get an abortion. In the parallel universes, she either doesn&#8217;t exist or her life is hopelessly boring. This leads to a pretty massive existential crisis, but she&#8217;s stopped by Morty, who has already had his fair share of timey-wimey weirdness.</p>\n<p>Morty takes Summer upstairs and shows her two dirt mounds in the backyard. He explains that he&#8217;s not the Morty from this timeline, and that he and Rick had to come here after things in their timeline got too bad. The Rick and Morty in this timeline had just died, so they slipped in unnoticed. Then, Morty gives Summer a bit of advice that shows he&#8217;s beginning to grow up a bit on his madcap adventures.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Nobody exists on purpose. Nobody belongs anywhere. Everybody’s gonna die. Come watch TV?&#8221; he pleads.</p>\n<p>The episode ends with the entire Smith family realizing that dwelling on possible alternate realities will only ever cause problems. It&#8217;s a testament to living in the here and now, and is one of the series&#8217; most emotionally resounding moments.</p>\n<p>There are dozens of shows with multiverse stories out there, from &#8217;90s sci-fi staple <em><strong>S</strong><strong>liders</strong></em><strong> </strong>to the later seasons of <strong><em>Supernatural</em>. </strong>These five, however, helped expand upon the trope as a whole, and are worth checking out to improve your pop culture savvy. That, and they&#8217;re just a lot of fun.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-multiverse-tv-episodes-guide/\">What is the Multiverse? Five Must-See Alternate Timeline TV Episodes to Watch After &#8216;Loki&#8217;</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"‘The Suicide Squad’ Director James Gunn Reflects on Being Temporarily Fired From ‘Guardians of the Galaxy 3’","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683701","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-513337\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/guardiansofthegalaxy-jamesgunn-davebautista-700x350.jpg\" alt=\"Suicide Squad 2 Cast\" width=\"700\" height=\"350\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/guardiansofthegalaxy-jamesgunn-davebautista.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/guardiansofthegalaxy-jamesgunn-davebautista-360x180.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Writer/director <strong>James Gunn&#8217;s</strong> ascent to blockbuster filmmaking hasn&#8217;t exactly been the smoothest one, to say the least. Many fans woke up one morning in July 2018 to the social media firestorm regarding Gunn and many wildly ill-advised tweets that were disingenuously unearthed by far-right commentators, posts that featured inappropriately crass jokes and made light of topics such as pedophilia and rape. The filmmaker, who only landed on Marvel&#8217;s radar in the first place thanks to his intentionally provocative work with schlocky B-movie studio Troma, <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/james-gunn-fired-guardians-of-the-galaxy-3/\">soon found himself fired</a> by Disney as a result of the backlash.</p>\n<p>Obviously, things have since improved for the controversial public figure. He subsequently added DC&#8217;s <em><strong>The Suicide Squad</strong></em> and its HBO Max spin-off series <em><strong>Peacemaker</strong></em> to his busy plate, followed soon after with <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/guardians-of-the-galaxy-vol-3-director-2/\">regaining his <em><strong>Guardians of the Galaxy: Volume 3</strong></em> gig</a>. Gunn has <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/guardians-of-the-galaxy-firing/\">taken responsibility and discussed these events</a> previously, but a new interview has him giving his most in-depth conversation on the topic yet.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683701\"></span></p>\n<p>Gunn&#8217;s frank and introspective comments throughout a wide-ranging interview with <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/07/14/movies/james-gunn-the-suicide-squad.html\">The New York Times</a> have the added effect of giving readers a glimpse into the behind-the-scenes process of any major studio, particularly when a high-profile employee finds themselves in hot water. Gunn describes the events of that day in detail, particularly the moment when he first realized that his tweets wouldn&#8217;t simply blow over and that his job was actually at risk:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;It was conveyed to me by <strong>Kevin Feige</strong> [the Marvel Studios president]. I called Kevin the morning it was going on, and I said, &#8216;Is this a big deal?&#8217; And he goes, &#8216;I don’t know.&#8217; That was a moment. I was like, &#8216;You don’t know?&#8217; I was surprised. Later he called me — he himself was in shock — and told me what the powers that be had decided. It was unbelievable. And for a day, it seemed like everything was gone. Everything was gone. I was going to have to sell my house. I was never going to be able to work again. That’s what it felt like.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>Obviously, any filmmaker or public figure in general who chooses to be active on social media runs the risk of posting the wrong thing at some point in time, having those posts exposed to a much wider audience, and then dealing with the inevitable consequences. That most definitely applies to Gunn, and he goes on to expand on what he&#8217;s learned, if anything, about choosing his words more carefully since then:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;Yes and no. I’m more considerate of people’s feelings today. I had talked about this a lot before those tweets were [resurfaced]. They are awful things, that’s what my sense of humor was back then. But before this ever happened, I realized that I had closed myself off to things I thought were schmaltzy because I didn’t want to be vulnerable. This attitude — I can make a joke about anything, look how great I am — that’s just not the fullness of me as a human being. And I learned that long before I got called out for the tweets.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-419427\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jamesgunn-groot-kevinfeige-guardiansride-700x351.jpg\" alt=\"Guardians of the Galaxy Ride\" width=\"700\" height=\"351\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jamesgunn-groot-kevinfeige-guardiansride-700x351.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jamesgunn-groot-kevinfeige-guardiansride-360x181.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/jamesgunn-groot-kevinfeige-guardiansride.jpg 960w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Reckoning With His Past</h2>\n<p>As far as public accountability goes, this feels like the most any of us could possibly ask of someone who&#8217;s made some blatant mistakes in their past. Gunn has previously apologized for his actions, but what&#8217;s more encouraging is that he seems to recognize that this is now an inextricable part of his story on the path towards self-growth.</p>\n<p>Complicating matters is the fact that, while certainly a self-inflicted problem to begin with, these posts were only brought to light by far-right reactionaries who jumped at the chance to silence a vocal political adversary. Along those lines, &#8220;Cancel culture&#8221; is an example of a specific slice of rhetoric that gets thrown around a lot these days, which Gunn was also asked about in regards to whether he considers himself a victim.</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;I understand people’s preoccupation with that term. But it’s such a bigger issue than that. Because cancel culture also is people like Harvey Weinstein, who should be canceled. People who have gotten canceled and then remain canceled — most of those people deserved that. The paparazzi are not just the people on the streets — they’re the people combing Twitter for any past sins. All of that sucks. It’s painful. But some of it is accountability. And that part of it is good. It’s just about finding that balance.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>Again, these answers at least come across as honest and straightforward. There is certainly a broader discussion that needs to continue when it comes to which types of public figures are allowed to enjoy a redemption story vs those who are not afforded the same benefit of the doubt. Individually, however, we all can make our own judgment over whether Gunn appears changed by his experience.</p>\n<p>The Times interview also explore many less fraught topics, such as when WB/DC came knocking at Gunn&#8217;s door to offer him Superman (the very Monday after his firing by Disney, in fact!) as well as why he never even considered including <strong>Jared Leto&#8217;s</strong> Joker in his <em>Suicide Squad</em> film (an exceedingly good call, in our opinion). <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/07/14/movies/james-gunn-the-suicide-squad.html\">Click through</a> to read it in full yourself.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/james-gunn-on-being-fired-from-guardians-of-the-galaxy-3/\">&#8216;The Suicide Squad&#8217; Director James Gunn Reflects on Being Temporarily Fired From &#8216;Guardians of the Galaxy 3&#8217;</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"‘Fear Street Part 3: 1666’ Trailer: Netflix’s Horror Trilogy Comes to an End, in the Past","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683668","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-trailer.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683687\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-trailer-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"fear street part 3 trailer\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-trailer-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-trailer-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-trailer-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-trailer.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>It&#8217;s all been leading to this. This week, the <strong><em>Fear Street</em></strong> trilogy comes to a close with <strong><em>Fear Street Part 3: 1666</em></strong>. And whatever you&#8217;ve thought of the trilogy so far, you have to admit it&#8217;s been an exciting event. So often now, streaming titles come and go. Whatever hype there is seems to fade after the initial release. But <em>Fear Street</em>&#8216;s unique strategy of releasing a new film every week has kept the conversation going, and helped make <em>Fear Street</em> one of the buzziest bits of entertainment this summer. <em>Fear Street Part 3: 1666</em> brings together all the threads (and surviving characters) from the previous two films while also going back in time to show us how all of this really began.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683668\"></span></p>\n<h2><strong>Fear Street Part 3: 1666 Trailer</strong></h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/dj3CXY8rKuY?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Just what the heck is going on in the cursed town of Shadyside? Why is neighboring Sunnyvale so prosperous? What does the alleged witch Sarah Fier want? Who will survive and what will be left of them? These questions may or may not be answered in <em>Fear Street Part 3: 1666</em>, the third and final entry in Netflix&#8217;s wildly entertaining <em>Fear Street</em> trilogy. Inspired by the work of R.L. Stine, the series has served as a fun tribute to the horror genre as a whole, with the first film <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/fear-street-part-1-1994-review/\">honoring the &#8217;90s slasher boom</a> trigged by <em>Scream</em> and the second film <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/fear-street-part-2-review/\">paying homage</a> to earlier slashers like <em>Friday the 13th</em>.</p>\n<p>Now, here comes <em>Fear Street Part 3: 1666</em>, and as you can tell from the title, it&#8217;s going back even further in time. In the ongoing &#8217;90s plotline, the curse of Sarah Fier is still a big problem for high schooler Deena (<strong>Kiana Madeira</strong>), especially since her girlfriend Sam (<strong>Olivia Scott Welch</strong>) is now possessed by the malevolent power that turns Shadysiders into crazed killers. Can Deena save Sam, and the town? Maybe – but first we&#8217;re getting some backstory set in the early days of Shadyside. As you can see from this trailer, many of the previous cast members return here, playing different characters in the 1600s. And as you can probably guess by now, there&#8217;s more to the Sarah Fier story than what meets the eye.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-1666-image.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683689\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-1666-image-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-1666-image-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-1666-image-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-1666-image-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-1666-image.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>The New World</strong></h2>\n<p>For this third entry, director<strong> Leigh Janiak</strong> drew on an unexpected source – a Terrence Malick movie. &#8220;As a filmmaker making<em> Fear Street</em>, but also just as a movie lover, I was so excited to pay homage to some of the great eras of horror movies,&#8221; Janiak said. &#8220;For 1994, <em>Scream</em> stood above all rest – it&#8217;s peak &#8217;90s horror and, I think, one of the most brilliant movies ever made, period. Then for 1978, I got to look at the heyday of slasher films — <em>Friday the 13th</em>, <em>Halloween</em>, <em>Nightmare on Elm Street</em>. For 1666&#8230;I found the best inspiration for me lay in the beautiful world made rotten of Terence Malick&#8217;s <em>The New World</em>.&#8221;</p>\n<p><em>Fear Street Part 3</em> features a cast that includes <strong>Kiana Madeira</strong>,<strong> Ashley Zukerman</strong>,<strong> Gillian Jacobs</strong>,<strong> Olivia Scott Welch</strong>,<strong> Benjamin Flores Jr.</strong>, <strong>Darrell Britt-Gibson</strong>, <strong>Sadie Sink</strong>,<strong> Emily Rudd</strong>,<strong> Mccabe Slye</strong>,<strong> Julia Rehwald</strong>,<strong> Fred Hechinger</strong>,<strong> Jordana Spiro</strong>,<strong> Jordyn Dinatale</strong>,<strong> Elizabeth Scopel</strong>, and<strong> Randy Havens</strong>. Look for it on Netflix on <strong>July 16</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/fear-street-part-3-trailer/\">&#8216;Fear Street Part 3: 1666&#8217; Trailer: Netflix&#8217;s Horror Trilogy Comes to an End, in the Past</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a +0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-trailer-700x321.jpg","linkMd5":"30188726c7f3e8afb0dc67a4339e15e2","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn4@2020_1/2021/07/14/17-33-37-539_16af5aeee540070a.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":321,"sourceBytes":14227,"destBytes":6242,"author":"Chris Evangelista","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-trailer-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn4@2020_1/2021/07/14/17-33-37-539_16af5aeee540070a.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/fear-street-part-3-1666-image-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn60@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-33-46-638_9cc339c447fad6f7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn40@2020_4/2021/07/14/17-33-46-881_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=fQBiq6L9tLU:QeqrNWvx7IY:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn63@2020_6/2021/07/14/17-33-46-226_66d79c036800411c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn92@2020_6/2021/07/14/17-33-47-600_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=fQBiq6L9tLU:QeqrNWvx7IY:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn7@2020_4/2021/07/14/17-33-47-251_44a37f5670f29878.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/fQBiq6L9tLU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn68@2020_5/2021/07/14/17-33-47-053_321638b8ef8756c9.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626284004433},{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"‘Loki’ Cast and Crew on Filming the Surprising Finale (and Keeping That Big Reveal a Secret)","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683669","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-680600 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Episode-4-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Episode-4-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Episode-4-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Episode-4-768x329.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Marvel</strong> does many things extraordinarily well, but the studio just might have no rival when it comes to preserving secrets and hiding massive character/casting reveals until the absolute last second (<a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/lukes-return-in-the-mandalorian/\">except maybe its Disney sibling, Lucasfilm</a>). The recently-concluded <em><strong>Loki</strong></em> continues this proud tradition, springing one of its biggest surprises yet during its finale. Fans can certainly count themselves as constantly impressed, but that&#8217;s nothing compared to the actual cast and crew involved in bringing <em>Loki</em> to life. For the sake of the spoiler-averse, we&#8217;ll save their quotes and reactions for further down below.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Major spoilers</strong> for the finale of </em>Loki<em> follow. Seriously. This is your last chance if you haven&#8217;t watched that final episode yet.</em></p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683669\"></span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-679715 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-timekeepers-poster-frontpage-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Loki Poster\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-timekeepers-poster-frontpage.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/loki-timekeepers-poster-frontpage-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Still here? Good, let&#8217;s get right to it.</p>\n<p>In the aftermath of the final episode, &#8220;For All Time. Always,&#8221; we&#8217;re left to ponder the multiverse-spanning ramifications of Sylvie (<strong>Sophia Di Martino</strong>) killing off <strong>Jonathan Majors&#8217;</strong> Kang the Conqueror, the all-powerful being revealed to have been behind the Time Variance Authority all along. But as all supervillains have a tendency to do, the mysterious &#8220;He Who Remains&#8221; is far from out of the picture for good. As explained to Sylvie and Loki (<strong>Tom Hiddleston</strong>) throughout the episode, he seemingly has an army of his own variants ready to step in and wreak some havoc.</p>\n<p>Rest assured, a studio doesn&#8217;t cast an actor as <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/creed-3-cast-jonathan-majors/\">in-demand as Majors</a> for a brief appearance in the finale of a Disney+ show.</p>\n<p>While we can only speculate on <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-season-2/\">what will happen next season</a>, <a href=\"https://www.marvel.com/articles/tv-shows/loki-he-who-remains-jonathan-majors\">Marvel.com</a> talked with the creators and cast of <em>Loki</em> to get their insights on everything that went into the decision to wrangle Majors for this role. Creator and writer <strong>Michael Waldron</strong> goes into detail about the new supervillain&#8217;s backstory, his place in the greater MCU, and generally all things Kang:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;We knew that we wanted this show to be huge, and we wanted it to really end with a bang and have a huge impact on the MCU moving forward. Knowing that Kang was probably going to be the next big cross-movie villain, and because he is a time-traveling, multiversal adversary, it just always made so much sense. I came up with that big multiversal war mythology and pitched it out in the room one day to our producers. And they said, yeah, let&#8217;s go for it. We knew we were going to end up meeting the man behind the curtain. And then it was just on us to make sure that that meeting really delivered.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>As director, <strong>Kate Herron</strong> had the pleasure of collaborating with Majors up close and personal on set. Fittingly enough, his presence ties the entire series together and embodies much of the show&#8217;s main ideas.</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;I was quite excited that we got to show him because he is the one that brings it all [together]. [He’s] the theme of our show. No one is completely good or completely bad, and people do fall into that gray area. I thought his reasoning with [Loki and Sylvie] that you can take me out, but I&#8217;ll be back here anyway&#8230;you&#8217;re going to awaken all these versions of me. And they are much scarier than me. I really believe him when he says that.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683640 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-768x329.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>The Jonathan Majors Effect</h2>\n<p>The reason so many were excited about <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/ant-man-3-villain/\">Majors&#8217; casting in the first place</a> mainly has to do with the amount of sheer charisma he brings to any role, which Marvel fans definitely got a taste of in the finale. Majors has enjoyed a much-deserved hot streak in the last few years, starring in the wonderfully understated <em><strong>The Last Black Man in San Francisco</strong></em>, <strong>Spike Lee&#8217;s <em>Da 5 Bloods</em></strong>, and the HBO series <em><strong>Lovecraft Country</strong></em>. As you might imagine, this screen presence factored in to just how to adapt the comic book villain Kang (whom Waldron describes as a &#8220;very charismatic sociopath&#8221;), toeing the line between being fun to watch and also genuinely up to no good, particularly when it comes to his variants.</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;You had to leave a lot of meat on the bone in terms of how evil he could be, because that&#8217;s He Who Remains&#8217; whole thing, that it&#8217;s not me who you should be afraid of. &#8216;It&#8217;s the other versions of me that are going to come.’ It was trying to really hint at that terrifying evil within without going all the way there.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>In response to Marvel pulling off yet another magic trick with Majors&#8217; casting, Waldron goes on to call it, &#8220;So exciting and humbling. You have such an astounding actor who is that much more of a cool thing. You had to write him in a way that he felt worthy of being the villain at the end of our show<em>.</em>&#8221; It&#8217;s safe to say that few others but Majors could pull off such a casually easy-going attitude while still playing a convincing Big Bad, and Waldron seems to agree. &#8220;I knew I could always breathe a sigh of relief knowing we had Majors in that finale. We hung a lot of our hopes on [the character]. This guy is laying out, ‘Here&#8217;s the deal,’ and it’s one final test between our two Lokis.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The universal adoration for Majors isn&#8217;t limited to the talent behind the camera, either. Hiddleston himself isn&#8217;t shy about heaping praise onto his villainous counterpart, as well:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;I just want to salute Jonathan Majors. He came in the last lap of this series and made an extraordinary impact. And it’s quite something to do that for a story, to get to its final chapter and to introduce the character of such breadth, and depth, and charisma, and intelligence. He was dazzling. It was our final week of filming, literally. He came in and blew us all away.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;It was so exciting for me to watch because I knew that for Jonathan, as an actor, it’s his entry point into the MCU. To watch him come in and be so ready, and so agile, and so prepared, and so surprising. Sophia and I sat and watched him deliver this extraordinary performance of such wit and with such intelligence. It was a real thrill to watch him do that.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>And according to co-star Di Martino, &#8220;He was so much fun and he absolutely blew it out of the park. As soon as he was on set, he was phenomenal. Like, no one could take their eyes off him. You knew something magical was happening and it was like, ‘Oh my god, are you watching this? This is going to be amazing.’&#8221;</p>\n<p>We could gush endlessly about Jonathan Majors, but fortunately he&#8217;s sure to be a fixture in the MCU for years to come. Keep an eye out for more of our <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-finale-review/\">coverage of <em>Loki</em></a>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-finale-reveals-cast-crew/\">&#8216;Loki&#8217; Cast and Crew on Filming the Surprising Finale (and Keeping That Big Reveal a Secret)</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=qDRn9VaSVro:aIC_gXXOmO8:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"‘Loki’ Season 2 Confirmed: Let’s Talk About What Could Happen Next","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683647","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683635 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Finale-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Finale-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Finale-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Finale-768x329.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Just like that, we&#8217;ve reached the end of the (time)line with <em><strong>Loki</strong></em> as another Disney+ MCU series has come and gone. This particular finale, titled &#8220;For All Time. Always,&#8221; may have left viewers wondering just how the various loose ends would be wrapped up in the future. Is that it for the series? Would we see those star-crossed variants, Sylvie (<strong>Sophia Di Martino</strong>) and Loki (<strong>Tom Hiddleston</strong>), pop up in future movies? Or maybe in another show altogether sometime down the line?</p>\n<p>The answer is&#8230;yes. <em>Loki</em> season 2 is coming. The first half of this article will be free of spoilers. The second half will be full of them.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683647\"></span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683649 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-season-2-700x291.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"291\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-season-2-700x291.png 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-season-2-360x150.png 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-season-2-768x319.png 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-season-2.png 1465w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Loki Season 2 Confirmed</h2>\n<p>Those who stuck around for the mid-credits scene had some questions properly laid to rest. After the final cliffhanger and a brief round of credits, we find ourselves right back at the offices of the Time Variance Authority that Loki first encountered in the series premiere. A familiar TVA stamp comes down onto Loki Laufeyson&#8217;s case file, but with a pretty major twist. &#8220;Loki will return in season 2,&#8221; reads the final teasing message. Yes, this officially confirms that the God(s) of Mischief will indeed have more adventures to come and more work to do while seeking their glorious purpose.</p>\n<p>Intriguingly, this is a stark departure from the precedent set by both previous Disney+ shows. <em><strong>WandaVision</strong></em>, which was billed as a limited series (and was <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/2021-emmy-nominations/\">nominated for its 23 Emmys</a> under this designation), set up <strong>Elizabeth Olsen&#8217;s</strong> Wanda Maximoff next appearance on the big screen in <em><strong>Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness</strong></em> rather than in another future season of the show. Meanwhile, news quickly broke after the finale of <em><strong>The Falcon and the Winter Soldier</strong></em> that <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/captain-america-4/\"><strong>Anthony Mackie</strong> would be leading a new <em>Captain America</em> movie</a> of his own. It&#8217;s understandable that fans may have expected more of the same with <em>Loki</em>.</p>\n<p>Instead, we&#8217;ll be seeing at least one more season of Loki and Sylvie on Disney+. Now, let&#8217;s get into the nitty gritty details about what this all could mean moving forward. Naturally, this involves talking <strong>spoilers</strong>.</p>\n<p><strong>Seriously</strong>.<strong> Major spoilers</strong> for the season finale of <em>Loki</em> lie ahead.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683640 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-768x329.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Looking Ahead</h2>\n<p>So, Sylvie did <em>that</em>. After confronting the overwhelming presence of Kang the Conqueror, the man behind the curtain played by the <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/ant-man-3-villain/\">previously-announced for the MCU <strong>Jonathan Majors</strong></a>, Sylvie finally takes her destiny into her hands and shockingly plunges her sword through his chest. This immediately sets off major changes throughout the so-called Sacred Timeline and fractures reality into infinite branches, the likes of which Mobius (<strong>Owen Wilson</strong>) and the TVA at large have never seen before.</p>\n<p>Can&#8217;t say she and Loki weren&#8217;t warned, though! For the bulk of the episode, Kang (who goes unnamed throughout the episode except for his cryptic title, &#8220;He Who Remains&#8221;) carefully and ponderously outlines just what limited choices the intrusive variants have at their disposal: kill him and set off another multiversal war as his own variants once again wrestle for control, or peacefully replace him as the new leaders of the TVA and enjoy a fantasy-fulfilling life at each other&#8217;s sides. Naturally, their disagreement over what to do next is resolved by a fight, a romantic kiss&#8230; and a prompt kick back to the TVA through time and space so Sylvie could do what (she thinks) needs to be done.</p>\n<p>So what now? When Loki finds Mobius and Hunter B-15 (<strong>Wunmi Mosaku</strong>), the damage already seems to be done. Neither even seems to recognize him, leading to the final reveal of a Kang statue dominating the TVA offices where the ones memorializing the Timekeepers used to reside. And that&#8217;s it! That&#8217;s the tantalizing image we&#8217;re left with, and we must simply wait and see when season 2 will drop.</p>\n<p>Obviously, Kang appears to be positioned as the next multi-film big bad in the MCU after Thanos was finally dispatched once and for all in <em><strong>Avengers: Endgame</strong></em>. No rest for the weary, huh? Though Kang seemingly bit the dust in the <em>Loki</em> finale, we&#8217;ll be seeing either him or some form of his variants (or both!) pop up in <em><strong>Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania</strong></em>. And then there&#8217;s <strong><em>Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness</em></strong>, whose title certainly implies that it will double down on the multiverse that was merely winked at in <em><strong>Spider-Man: Far From Home</strong></em>.</p>\n<p>The MCU has taken pains to connect the Quantum Realm with the steadily-expanding multiverse, so brush up on your MCU continuity and be ready for these all-important feature films in the MCU. In the meantime, be sure to stay tuned to /Film as we scrutinize every inch of this <em>Loki</em> finale.</p>\n<p><em>Doctor Strange in the Multiverse of Madness</em> will release in theaters on <strong>March 25, 2022</strong>. The wait for <em>Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania</em> will be a bit longer, as it&#8217;s currently set for <strong>February 17, 2023</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-season-2/\">&#8216;Loki&#8217; Season 2 Confirmed: Let&#8217;s Talk About What Could Happen Next</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=WzqPx4T4DmU:JtGTTkhpB-M:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img 01:33:24","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:24","title":"Who is “He Who Remains?” Breaking Down the Bombshell Appearance in the ‘Loki’ Season Finale","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683633","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-683659 size-medium\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/arc-106-18739_r2_12f8915f-e1626270910217-700x302.jpeg\" alt=\"Who is the Loki Villain\" width=\"700\" height=\"302\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/arc-106-18739_r2_12f8915f-e1626270910217.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/arc-106-18739_r2_12f8915f-e1626270910217-360x155.jpeg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Alright, Marvelites. Whose brain is melted after <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-finale-review/\">watching the season finale</a> of <strong><em>Loki</em></strong>? The episode peels back the curtain on the show&#8217;s big bad, and already it feels like we&#8217;re dancing around <strong>major spoilers</strong>. So if you haven&#8217;t seen the finale yet, by all means, go watch it on <strong>Disney+ </strong>and then come back here and let&#8217;s talk about who this character is and what their appearance might mean for Phase 4 of the Marvel Cinematic Universe.</p>\n<p>All other variants: please proceed to the next TVA checkpoint.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683633\"></span></p>\n<p>This is your final warning: <strong>spoilers</strong> for <em>Loki</em>, Season 1, Episode 6, &#8220;For All Time. Always,&#8221; follow below.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683639 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Miss-Minutes-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Miss-Minutes-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Miss-Minutes-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Miss-Minutes-768x329.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>So Long, Lovecraft Country. Hello, Kang Country</h2>\n<p>It turns out that <em>Loki</em> makes use of not one, but two alumni of HBO&#8217;s <em>Lovecraft Country</em>. Sadly, that show was <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/lovecraft-country-cacnceled-at-hbo/\">unceremoniously canceled</a> this month, but we&#8217;ve already seen <strong>Wunmi Mosaku </strong>portray Hunter B-15 on <em>Loki</em>. Now, she&#8217;s joined by her <em>Lovecraft Country </em>co-star <strong>Jonathan Majors</strong>, who appears in <em>Loki</em>&#8216;s season finale as the mysterious &#8220;He Who Remains&#8221; in the <a href=\"https://www.marvel.com/articles/tv-shows/loki-he-who-remains-citadel-end-of-time-kang-statue\">Citadel at the End of Time</a>. The door slides open and he&#8217;s sitting there in his lounge chair, holding a green apple, as if this were the Garden of Eden and he was the serpent, there to tempt Adam and Eve (or in this case, <strong>Tom Hiddleston</strong>&#8216;s Loki and <strong>Sophia Di Martino</strong>&#8216;s Sylvie). A big smile spreads across his face and he stands up and says, &#8220;This is wild.&#8221;</p>\n<p>It sure is. If you are or ever have been a comic book reader, the appearance of Majors in <em>Loki</em> is one of those moments that might take you back to the Wednesday afternoon thrill of a new issue where some mind-blowing twist was delivered. This is part of the joy of serialized storytelling, whether it be comics or TV or shared movie universes.</p>\n<p>We already knew that Majors had been <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/ant-man-3-villain/\">cast as major Marvel villain <strong>Kang the Conqueror</strong></a> in <em>Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania</em>, and there have been Kang Easter eggs in <em>Loki</em> since <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-episode-1-easter-eggs/\">the very first episode.</a> Knowing Marvel Studios&#8217; history of mid-credits and post-credits teases, it was reasonable to assume that we might get something like that with Kang at the end of <em>Loki</em>. But that&#8217;s just it: <em>Loki</em>, the series, hasn&#8217;t ended yet. The mid-tease credits tease that we do get here is a stamp on Loki&#8217;s case file in the offices of the Time Variance Authority, telling us that <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/loki-season-2/\">&#8220;Loki will return in Season 2.&#8221;</a></p>\n<p>Majors, meanwhile, winds up having a much bigger role to play in the finale, so much so that he almost hijacks Loki&#8217;s show for a few minutes as he sits behinds his desk and explains his &#8220;gambit&#8221; through expository dialogue. He&#8217;s never explicitly named as Kang, and in fact, his appearance is more like that of Immortus, an alternate version of Kang in the comics.</p>\n<p>About that …</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683640 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Jonathan-Majors-768x329.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Jonathan Majors Could Be Both Immortus and Kang</h2>\n<p>Immortus didn&#8217;t wear a mask, just a funny hat, purple cape, and green robes. Majors doesn&#8217;t have the hat but he does have the cape and colors. He immediately makes an impression as a much zanier, more vamping Immortus or Kang than we ever saw in the comics. At one point, he even jumps up on a piece of furniture like he&#8217;s Tom Cruise on <em>The Oprah Winfrey Show</em>.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Don&#8217;t tell me I&#8217;m a disappointment,&#8221; he says. It&#8217;s as if he&#8217;s reading the minds of hardcore Kang fans, who might be disappointed to see yet another classic Marvel villain rendered maskless in the MCU. Daniel Bruhl&#8217;s Baron Zemo did finally don his ski mask this year in <em>The Falcon and the Winter Soldier</em>, but it was only for one scene, and the MCU has a history of leaving the masks off other villains, like the Shocker in <em>Spider-Man: Homecoming</em>. But I digress.</p>\n<p>As his name implies, Kang the Conqueror is a warlord in the comics. He&#8217;s a time-traveler from the year 3000 (we love him 3000?) and Immortus is his older self. The two characters fought on opposite sides in the <em>Avengers Forever</em> mini-series, a series that also notably featured the Time Keepers. Before <em>Loki</em>&#8216;s premiere, <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/who-are-the-timekeepers/\">we speculated</a>, based on the first two episodes, that the show could be &#8220;grafting part of the comics story of Kang and Immortus onto <em>Loki</em>.&#8221;</p>\n<p>That is exactly what it has done. In the same article linked above, we also speculated that the Time Keepers could be major power players in the MCU going forward. As it turns out, the joke was on us there: the Time Keepers were nothing more than &#8220;robotic puppets,&#8221; as <a href=\"https://www.marvel.com/articles/tv-shows/loki-he-who-remains-jonathan-majors\">Marvel.com</a> calls them. He Who Remains was the one pulling the strings. That major power player the show was setting up was, well, Jonathan Majors&#8217; Kang. <em>Loki</em> does utilize more of the comic book backstory for the Time Keepers, however, when it takes us into the aforementioned Citadel at the End of Time and introduces us to the first and last Time Keeper.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683673 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Kang-Statue-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Kang-Statue-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Kang-Statue-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Loki-Season-1-Finale-Kang-Statue-768x329.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Kang Could Also Open the Door to the Fantastic Four</h2>\n<p>In <em>Loki</em>, we&#8217;ve now seen multiple variants of the god of mischief, including <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/alligator-loki/\">an alligator</a>. The info dump that He Who Remains delivers in the season finale (can we just call him Kang, for the sake of convenience?) reveals that there have been other, more dangerous variants of him, too. This one is the glue holding together the Sacred Timeline, and if Sylvie kills him, which she does, it could open the door to a whole universe (multiverse?) of trouble in the form of other Kangs.</p>\n<p>In the comics, another version of Kang goes by the name of Nathaniel Richards. That&#8217;s not the same Nathaniel Richards who is the grandfather of Reed Richards, AKA Mr. Fantastic, the leader of the Fantastic Four. However, the character could be a descendent of the same man, which would give him a viable connection to Marvel&#8217;s First Family. <em>Spider-Man: Far from Home</em> director Jon Watts is <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/new-fantastic-four-movie/\">already attached</a> to a new Fantastic Four movie from Marvel Studios, so we know the FF is on the way in the MCU. Given the overlap between Kang and the Fantastic Four in the comics, it would make sense for him to help introduce them in the movies.</p>\n<p>There&#8217;s also Kang&#8217;s status as a Thanos-level threat, someone capable of mucking with the temporal fabric of reality and the fate of all our heroes. Thanos got a post-credits tease in <em>The Avengers</em> back in 2012, and he made an appearance in <em>Guardians of the Galaxy</em> in 2014, but it wasn&#8217;t until six years after his onscreen debut that Marvel Studios finally fleshed him out as a full villain (on his own twisted, genocidal hero&#8217;s quest) in <em>Avengers: Infinity War</em>.</p>\n<p>With Majors already locked in for <em>Ant-Man and the Wasp: Quantumania </em>in 2023, it&#8217;s probably safe to expect that Kang will have a more active and immediate presence in Phase 4 of the MCU than Thanos did in Phase 2. In the comics, the character also has history with <strong>Gugu</strong> <strong>Mbatha-Raw</strong>&#8216;s character, Ravonna Renslayer. They&#8217;ve been both lovers and enemies, so odds are strong they&#8217;ll be meeting in the movies or the show, too.</p>\n<p><em>Loki</em>&#8216;s season 1 finale sees the Sacred Timeline branching off into a true multiverse (<a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/tag/doctor-strange-in-the-multiverse-of-madness/\">of madness</a>). It leaves him marooned in a reality where Mobius (<strong>Owen Wilson</strong>) doesn&#8217;t know who he is, and where the statue of Kang stands in the atrium of the TVA in place of the Time Keepers. Mark that statue and mark its likeness, because it&#8217;s an important new face that you&#8217;ll be seeing more of in the MCU in the years to come.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/who-is-the-loki-villain/\">Who is &#8220;He Who Remains?&#8221; Breaking Down the Bombshell Appearance in the &#8216;Loki&#8217; Season Finale</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=Uf01YnVnE3k:XBEjvO8HWOI:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img
